### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The area of a triangle can be calculated as (1/2) * base * height.
  The two triangles created by cutting a rectangle diagonally are congruent.
  If the area of a triangle is 70 square feet, then the base and height must multiply to 140 square feet.
  If the original piece of cloth was a square, then all four sides were equal in length.

Action: 
  Let x be the length of one side of the original square piece of cloth.
  After trimming, the rectangular piece has dimensions x-4 by x.
  The area of the rectangular piece is (x-4)x = x^2 - 4x.
  The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so the base and height of each triangle are both sqrt(140/x).
  The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x.
  We can set up an equation using the Pythagorean Theorem to solve for x:
  (x-4)^2 + x^2 = (2sqrt(140/x))^2
  Simplifying this equation gives us:
  2x^2 - 16x - 560 = 0
  Solving for x using the quadratic formula gives us:
  x = 14 or x = -20
  Since x must be positive, we can discard the negative solution.
  The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x = 56.

Answer: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle is given by the formula A = (1/2)bh, where b is the base and h is the height.
  - The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so we can use this information to find the dimensions of the rectangular piece of cloth.
  - If we let x be the length of the rectangular piece, then the width is x - 4 (since 4 feet was trimmed from one edge).
  - The area of the rectangle is then x(x - 4) = x^2 - 4x square feet.
  - We can use the Pythagorean theorem to find the length of the diagonal of the rectangle, which is also the hypotenuse of each triangle.
  - The Pythagorean theorem states that for a right triangle with legs of length a and b and hypotenuse of length c, we have c^2 = a^2 + b^2.
  - In this case, the legs of each triangle are x - 4 and h, where h is the height of the triangle.
  - We know that the area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so we can solve for h using the formula A = (1/2)bh.
  - Once we know h, we can use the Pythagorean theorem to find the length of the hypotenuse, which is also the diagonal of the rectangle.
  - Finally, we can add up the dimensions of the rectangle and the length of the diagonal to find the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth.

Action: Answer("D")  
Solution:
  - Let x be the length of the rectangular piece, then the width is x - 4.
  - The area of the rectangle is x(x - 4) = x^2 - 4x square feet.
  - Since the area of each triangle is 70 square feet, we have (1/2)(x - 4)h = 70, where h is the height of each triangle.
  - Solving for h, we get h = 140/(x - 4).
  - Using the Pythagorean theorem, we have (x - 4)^2 + h^2 = d^2, where d is the length of the diagonal of the rectangle.
  - Substituting for h, we get (x - 4)^2 + (140/(x - 4))^2 = d^2.
  - Simplifying, we get x^4 - 8x^3 + 2320x - 62720 = 0.
  - This equation factors as (x - 20)(x^3 + 12x^2 - 240x + 3136) = 0.
  - The only positive root of the cubic factor is approximately 6.8, so x = 20.
  - Therefore, the dimensions of the rectangle are 20 feet by 16 feet, and the length of the diagonal (and hypotenuse of each triangle) is sqrt(20^2 + 16^2) = 4sqrt(41) feet.
  - The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4 times the length of a side, which is 20 feet, plus the length of the diagonal, which is 4sqrt(41) feet.
  - Therefore, the perimeter is approximately 62 feet. Answer: D.

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The painted sides are two adjacent sides and one end of the rectangle.
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangle is l and the width is w.
  The unpainted side is the other end of the rectangle, which has length 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, so we can write an equation: l + 2w = 37.
  The area of the rectangle is A = lw.

Action: 
  We can solve for l in the equation l + 2w = 37: l = 37 - 2w.
  Substituting this expression for l into the equation for the area, we get A = w(37 - 2w) = 37w - 2w^2.
  To maximize the area, we can take the derivative of A with respect to w, set it equal to zero, and solve for w: dA/dw = 37 - 4w = 0, so w = 9.25.
  Plugging this value of w into the equation for l, we get l = 37 - 2(9.25) = 18.5.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangle is A = lw = 9.25 * 18.5 = 170.875 square feet, which is closest to answer C.

Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = l * w, where l is the length and w is the width.
  If three sides of a rectangle are painted, then the unpainted side is opposite to the painted side that is not adjacent to it.
  Let w be the width of the parking space, then the length of the painted sides is 2w + 9.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, so 2w + 9 = 37 - w, which gives w = 14.
Action: Answer("A")

  LW = A

Question: Julies yard is rectangular. One side of the yard is 100 feet wide. The total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet. What is the length of the other side of the yard?
Choices:
  A: 30 feet
  B: 20 feet
  C: 10 feet
  D: 50 feet
  E: 60 feet
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is calculated by multiplying its length by its width.
  We know the width of the yard is 100 feet and the area of the yard is 3,000 square feet.
  To find the length of the yard, we can divide the area by the width.

Calculation:
  Length = Area / Width
  Length = 3,000 / 100
  Length = 30

Action: Answer("A") 
The length of the other side of the yard is 30 feet. Therefore, the correct answer is A.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 63 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that hose A can fill the entire pool in x hours, then its rate is 1/x. 
  Let's assume that hose B can fill the entire pool in y hours, then its rate is 1/y.
  If hose A can fill the pool alone in 8 hours, then its rate is 1/8.
  Using the formula: rate = work/time, we can set up the following equation:
  2*(1/8) + 3*(1/8 + 1/y) = 1
  The first term represents the work done by hose A in 2 hours, and the second term represents the work done by both hoses in 3 hours.
  We can simplify the equation to solve for y.

Action: Answer("B")  
Solution:
  2*(1/8) + 3*(1/8 + 1/y) = 1
  1/4 + 3/8 + 3/y = 1
  3/y = 1/8
  y = 24
  Therefore, hose B can fill the entire pool alone in 24 hours. 
  Answer: B
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that the rate of hose A is a and the rate of hose B is b. 
  We can use the formula: rate = work / time
  We can also use the formula: work = rate * time
  If hose A can fill the pool in 8 hours, then its rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour.
  If hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, then it completed 2/8 or 1/4 of the pool.
  If the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours, then they completed 3/8 of the pool.
  We can set up the equation: 
    1/4 + (a+b)*3/8 = 1
    Simplifying the equation, we get:
    a + b = 1/2
  We need to find how many hours it would have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool.
  Let's set up the equation:
    b * time = 3/8
    Solving for time, we get:
    time = (3/8) / b = 3 / (8b)
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that hose A can fill the entire pool in x hours. Therefore, the rate of hose A is 1/x of the pool per hour. 
  Let's assume that hose B can fill the entire pool in y hours. Therefore, the rate of hose B is 1/y of the pool per hour. 
  When both hoses work together, their rates add up. Therefore, the combined rate is 1/x + 1/y of the pool per hour. 
  We can use the formula: rate = work / time, where work is the amount of work done (in this case, filling the entire pool), and time is the time taken to do the work. 
  We can also use the formula: work = rate x time. 
  From the problem, we know that hose A can fill the entire pool in 8 hours. Therefore, the rate of hose A is 1/8 of the pool per hour. 
  Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours. Therefore, the amount of work done by hose A alone is (1/8) x 2 = 1/4 of the pool. 
  The remaining amount of work to be done is 1 - 1/4 = 3/4 of the pool. 
  Hose A and hose B worked together to fill the remaining 3/4 of the pool. Therefore, we can use the formula: (1/x + 1/y) x 3 = 3/4. 
  Simplifying this equation, we get: (1/x + 1/y) = 1/4. 
  We want to find the time taken by hose B to fill the entire pool, which is y. 

Action: Answer("C")  
  Using the equation (1/x + 1/y) = 1/4, we can substitute x = 8 (since hose A can fill the entire pool in 8 hours). 
  Therefore, we get: (1/8 + 1/y) = 1/4. 
  Simplifying this equation, we get: 1/y = 1/4 - 1/8 = 1/8. 
  Therefore, y = 8/1 = 8. 
  So, it would take hose B, working alone, 8 hours to fill the entire pool.

  (A + B) * 3 = 3/4

  B = 1/4 - A

  t = 4 / (4 - 4A)

  1/4 + 3/4 = 1
  A = 1/8
  B = 1/4 - A = 1/4 - 1/8 = 1/8
  t = 4 / (4 - 4A) = 4 / (4 - 4/8) = 8

Topic: Math
Question: Two numbers are in the ratio 3:5. If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are in the ratio 12:23. The smaller number is?
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be written as ax and bx, where x is a common factor and a and b are the given ratio.
  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the new numbers can be written as (ax - 9) and (bx - 9).
  If (ax - 9) and (bx - 9) are in the ratio c:d, then (ax - 9)/c = (bx - 9)/d.
  
Solution:
  Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x.
  Then, (3x - 9)/(5x - 9) = 12/23.
  Solving for x, we get x = 69.
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 207.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x.
  If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are 3x - 9 and 5x - 9.
  We are given that (3x - 9)/(5x - 9) = 12/23.
  We can use this equation to solve for x and then find the smaller number, which is 3x.
Action: 
  (3x - 9)/(5x - 9) = 12/23
  69x - 207 = 60x - 108
  9x = 99
  x = 11
  So the smaller number is 3x = 33.
  Answer("B")

Topic: Math
Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation is of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  If one of the roots of a quadratic equation is known, then the other root can be found by dividing c/a by the known root and then subtracting the result from the sum of the roots.
  
Let's use the above knowledge to solve the problem:
  The given quadratic equation is x^2 + mx + 22 = 0.
  One of the roots is given as 1.5.
  Therefore, the other root can be found as follows:
    Sum of the roots = -m/1 = -m
    Product of the roots = 22/1 = 22
    Other root = (Product of the roots) / (Known root) = 22 / 1.5 = 14.67
    Sum of the roots = (Known root) + (Other root) = 1.5 + 14.67 = 16.17
    Therefore, -m = 16.17
    m = -16.17
    
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation in standard form is ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  
Let's solve the problem:
  We know that one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5.
  Let's assume that the other root is r.
  The sum of the roots is 1.5 + r = -m/1.
  The product of the roots is 1.5r = 22/1.
  We can solve for r by dividing both sides of the equation by 1.5: r = 22/1.5 = 14.67.
  We can solve for m by substituting the values of the roots: 1.5 + 14.67 = -m/1.
  Solving for m: m = -16.17.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - In 2001, 300 deer were tagged and released.
  - In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
  - The percentage of deer with tags in the sample of 500 is assumed to be representative of the percentage of deer with tags in the entire population.
  - We can use proportions to solve the problem.
  
Solution:
  Let x be the total deer population in the forest.
  The proportion of deer with tags in the population is equal to the proportion of deer with tags in the sample:
  (number of deer with tags in the sample) / (total number of deer in the sample) = (number of deer with tags in the population) / (total number of deer in the population)
  We know that 20 deer in the sample had tags, so the number of deer with tags in the sample is 20.
  The total number of deer in the sample is 500.
  We don't know the number of deer with tags in the population, but we can express it in terms of x:
  (20 / 500) = (number of deer with tags in the population) / x
  Solving for the number of deer with tags in the population:
  number of deer with tags in the population = (20 / 500) * x
  In 2001, 300 deer were tagged, so the number of deer with tags in the population in 2002 is 300.
  We can set the two expressions for the number of deer with tags in the population equal to each other and solve for x:
  (20 / 500) * x = 300
  x = (300 * 500) / 20
  x = 7500
  Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7500.
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - In 2001, 300 deer were tagged.
  - In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
  - The percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags.
  - We can use proportions to solve the problem.
  
Solution:

The proportion of tagged deer in the forest before the second year is 300/x.
The proportion of tagged deer in the sample of 500 deer is 20/500 = 0.04.
Since the percent of tagged deer in the sample is representative of the percent of tagged deer in the forest, we can set up the following proportion:
300/x = 0.04
Solving for x, we get:
x = 300/0.04 = 7500

Question: In an exam, a candidate secured 504 marks of the maximum mark of M. If the maximum mark M is converted into 800 marks, he would have secured 420 marks. What is the value of M?
Choices:
  A: 278
  B: 2890
  C: 270
  D: 2702
  E: 960

  The candidate secured 504 marks out of x.
  If x is converted into 800 marks, he would have secured 420 marks.
  We can form two equations from the given information:
    504/x = 420/800
    x = ?
  We can solve for x using the above equations.
Action: Answer("E")  
Solution:

  504*800 = 420*x
  x = (504*800)/420
  x = 960
  Therefore, the value of M is 960. Answer: E

Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers leave the same remainder when divided by a third number, then their difference is divisible by that third number.
  If a number is divisible by 3, then the sum of its digits is also divisible by 3.
  If a number is divisible by 2, then its last digit is even.
  
Solution:
Let the 3-digit number be N and let the common remainder be R. Then we have:
  2272 = Nq + R
  875 = Nr + R
where q and r are the quotients and remainders when 2272 is divided by N, and when 875 is divided by N, respectively.
Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get:
  1397 = Nq - Nr
Since N divides both sides of this equation, it also divides 1397. The prime factorization of 1397 is 1397 = 19 x 73. Therefore, N can be any factor of 1397, except 1, 19, and 73. In particular, N is a 3-digit number, so it must be between 100 and 999.
The sum of the digits of N is divisible by 3, so we can eliminate choices A and D. The last digit of N is even, so we can eliminate choice E. That leaves us with choices B and C.
The sum of the digits of 731 is 11, which is choice B. We can check that this works:
  2272 = 3 x 731 + 79
  875 = 1 x 731 + 144
Both quotients leave a remainder of 79 when divided by 731, so the answer is B.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, then his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  If Jack finishes two-thirds of the work, then the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill to complete.
  If Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate, then her rate of cleaning is 5/100 * 1/12 = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  Let's assume that it takes Jill x hours to finish the remaining one-third of the work.
  We can use the formula: rate * time = work to solve for x.

Calculation:
  Jack's rate of cleaning = 1/12 of the yacht per hour
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill to complete.
  Jill's rate of cleaning = 5/100 * 1/12 = 1/240 of the yacht per hour
  Let's assume that it takes Jill x hours to finish the remaining one-third of the work.
  Jack's portion of the work = (2/3) * 1 = 2/3
  Jill's portion of the work = (1/3) * 1 = 1/3
  We can use the formula: rate * time = work to solve for x.
  Jack's work = Jack's rate * Jack's time = (1/12) * (2/3) = 1/18
  Jill's work = Jill's rate * Jill's time = (1/240) * x
  Total work = Jack's work + Jill's work = 1/18 + (1/240) * x = 1
  Solving for x, we get x = 20.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, so his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining portion of the work is one-third of the yacht.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate of cleaning, so her rate of cleaning is 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  We can use the formula: rate = work / time to solve the problem.
  Let t be the time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work.
  The work done by Jill is (1/3) of the yacht, so we have:
  (1/240) * t * yacht = (1/3) * yacht
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  t = (1/3) * 240 = 80
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, so his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  - Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill.
  - Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate of cleaning, which means her rate is (5/100) * (1/12) = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  - We need to find how long it takes Jill to finish the remaining one-third of the work.

Solution:
  - Let's assume the total work is represented by the number 1.
  - Jack finished two-thirds of the work, which means he did (2/3) of the work, leaving (1/3) of the work for Jill.
  - Let's call the time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work "t".
  - Jill's rate of cleaning is 1/240 of the yacht per hour, so in "t" hours, she can clean (1/240)*t of the yacht.
  - Since Jack finished two-thirds of the work, that means (1/3) of the work is left for Jill, which is equal to (1/3) of the yacht.
  - We can set up an equation to solve for "t":
      (1/240)*t = (1/3)
  - Solving for "t":
      t = (1/3) * 240
      t = 80
  - Therefore, it takes Jill 80 hours to finish the remaining one-third of the work.

  (2/3) of the yacht = (1/12) x (2/3) of the yacht + (1/20) x W

  W = (2/3) of the yacht - (1/12) x (2/3) of the yacht
  W = (4/9) of the yacht

  W = (Jill's rate of cleaning) x (time Jill worked)
  (4/9) of the yacht = (1/20) x t
  t = (4/9) of the yacht / (1/20)
  t = (4/9) x 20

Topic: Math
Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Let's call the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train "x". Then, the time it takes him to return by car would also be "x" since the distance is the same. 

According to the problem, if he goes both ways by train, it takes him 4 hours longer. So the total time for the round trip by train would be 2x + 4. 

We also know that the total time for the round trip by train and car is 17 hours. So we can set up the equation: 

2x + 4 + x = 17 

Simplifying, we get: 

3x + 4 = 17 

Subtracting 4 from both sides: 

3x = 13 

Dividing by 3: 

x = 4.33 

So it takes Mr. Sam 4.33 hours to travel to the city by train. 

If he traveled by car both ways, the total time would be twice the time it takes him to travel one way: 

2 * 4.33 = 8.66 

Rounding to the nearest hour, we get: 

Action: Answer("D") 20 hrs
Response 1:
Let's call the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train "x". 

According to the problem, it takes him 17 hours to go by train to the city and return by car. This means that the time it takes him to return by car is also 17 hours. 

If he loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train, then it would take him x+17+x+17-4=2x+30 hours to make the round trip by train. 

We want to know how long it would take him if he had traveled by car in both ways. This means he would spend 2x hours traveling (x hours to get to the city and x hours to return). 

We can set up an equation: 

2x = 2x + 30 - 17 

Simplifying: 

2x = 13 

x = 6.5 

So it takes Mr. Sam 6.5 hours to travel to the city by train. 

To find out how long it would take him if he had traveled by car in both ways, we add up the time it takes him to go to the city by car and the time it takes him to return by car: 

2(17) = 34 

Action: Answer("D") - 20 hrs

Knowledge:
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to go to the city by train is t1 and the time taken by him to return by car is t2.
  According to the problem, t1 + t2 = 17 and t1-4 = t2
  We need to find the time taken by Mr. Sam if he had traveled by car in both ways.
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel by car in both ways is t.
  We know that the distance traveled by Mr. Sam is the same in all cases.
  Therefore, the time taken to travel by car in both ways will be half of the time taken to go by train and return by car.
  That is, t = (t1 + t2)/2 = (17 + t1-4)/2 = (t1+13)/2
  Solving the above equation, we get t1 = 18.
  Therefore, t2 = t1-4 = 14.
  The time taken by Mr. Sam if he had traveled by car in both ways will be 2*t2 = 28.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 71 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the number of copper coins is "x" and the number of brass coins is "y".
  The amount of money the diver gets for each copper coin is 20 cents.
  The amount of money the diver gets for each brass coin is 25 cents.
  The total amount of money the diver got after one dive is $3.40.
  The equation that represents the total amount of money the diver got is: 0.20x + 0.25y = 3.40
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that she brought, so we need to minimize the value of "x".
  
Solution:
  We can start by simplifying the equation: 20x + 25y = 340
  We can divide both sides by 5: 4x + 5y = 68
  We know that "x" has to be an integer, so we can try different values of "x" to see which one gives us an integer value for "y":
  - If x = 1, then y = (68 - 4)/5 = 13.2 (not an integer)
  - If x = 2, then y = (68 - 8)/5 = 12 (an integer)
  - If x = 3, then y = (68 - 12)/5 = 11.2 (not an integer)
  - If x = 4, then y = (68 - 16)/5 = 10.4 (not an integer)
  - If x = 5, then y = (68 - 20)/5 = 9.6 (not an integer)
  - If x = 6, then y = (68 - 24)/5 = 8.8 (not an integer)
  - If x = 7, then y = (68 - 28)/5 = 8 (an integer)
  The minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 2 (choice C).
Action: Answer("C")

  We can set up the following equation: 0.20x + 0.25y = 3.40
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that she brought, which means we need to minimize the value of x.

Solution:
  We can solve the equation 0.20x + 0.25y = 3.40 for x in terms of y:
  0.20x = 3.40 - 0.25y
  x = (3.40 - 0.25y) / 0.20
  We want to find the minimum value of x, which means we want to find the smallest integer value of y that makes x an integer.
  We can try different values of y starting from 1 until we find an integer value of x.
  If y = 1, then x = (3.40 - 0.25) / 0.20 = 16, which is an integer.
  Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 16, and the number of brass coins is 1.
  Answer: A(4)

Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Let the three digit number be represented by ABC, where A, B, and C are the digits. 

From the first condition, we know that A + B + C = 17. 

From the second condition, we know that A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109. 

Let's try to find the value of the number ABC. 

We know that 100A + 10B + C = ABC. 

If we subtract 495 from this number, we get: 

100A + 10B + C - 495 = 100C + 10B + A 

Simplifying this equation, we get: 

99A - 99C = 495 

Dividing both sides by 99, we get: 

A - C = 5 

Now we have two equations: 

A + B + C = 17 

A - C = 5 

Solving for A, B, and C, we get: 

A = 6, B = 5, C = 6 

Therefore, the number ABC is 656.

  The volume of a cube with edge length a is given by V_cube = a^3.
  The volume of a sphere with radius r is given by V_sphere = (4/3)r^3.
  If a sphere is inscribed in a cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube, so the radius of the sphere is r = (1/2)a.
  The ratio of two volumes can be found by dividing one volume by the other.
  
Calculations:
  Let a be the edge length of the cube.
  The diameter of the inscribed sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube, so the radius of the sphere is r = (1/2)a.
  The volume of the cube is V_cube = a^3.
  The volume of the sphere is V_sphere = (4/3)r^3 = (4/3)(1/2a)^3 = (1/6)a^3.
  The ratio of the volumes is V_cube/V_sphere = a^3/[(1/6)a^3] = (6/).

Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  This is a combination problem because the order of the groups does not matter.
  The formula for the combination is nCr = n! / (r! * (n-r)!), where n is the total number of items, and r is the number of items to be selected.
  
Action: 
  We need to select 5 lime soda bottles out of 10 for the first group, and the remaining 5 bottles will go to the second group. 
  Therefore, the number of ways to create these 2 groups is:
  10C5 = 10! / (5! * (10-5)!) = 252
  Answer: Answer("D")

Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by a worm.
  - Let B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that V + W - B = 250 (since all files are either infected by a virus or a worm or both).
  - We also know that W = 2.5B (since the number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm).
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V = 0.5(250) = 125.
Action: 
  - We can substitute V = 125 and W = 2.5B into the equation V + W - B = 250 to get 125 + 2.5B - B = 250.
  - Solving for B, we get B = 50.
  - We can then substitute B = 50 into the equation W = 2.5B to get W = 125.
  - Finally, the number of files that were not infected by a worm is 250 - W = 250 - 125 = 125.
  - Answer: Answer("E")

Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus only.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by a worm only.

  - We also know that W = 2.5B.
  - We want to find the number of files that were not infected by a worm.
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V + B = 0.5(250) = 125.

    W = 250 - V - B
  - We can substitute W = 2.5B into the equation above to get:
    2.5B = 250 - V - B
    3.5B = 250 - V
    B = (250 - V) / 3.5
  - We can substitute V + B = 125 into the equation above to get:
    V + (250 - V) / 3.5 = 125
    3.5V + 250 - V = 437.5
    2.5V = 187.5
    V = 75

    B = 50
  - We can use W = 2.5B to get:
    W = 125
  - The number of files that were not infected by a worm is V, which is 75.

    - Therefore, the endpoints of the feasible region are B = 0 and B = 100.
    - Plugging in B = 0, we get V + U = 1000, which is not a choice.
    - Plugging in B = 100, we get V + U = 50, which is choice A.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 77 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Profit% = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit

Let CP be the cost price of the article.
Given, Profit% = 20% and Selling Price = Rs.360
Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
Profit = 360 - CP

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday.
  The hotel buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel pays $4 for each Sunday newspaper and $1 for each newspaper on the rest of the days of the week.
  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  The equation that represents the total cost of newspapers per week is: 4(2x) + 1(7x) = 210
  Solving this equation, we get: x = 15
  Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday, and 2x = 30 newspapers on Sunday.

Action: Answer("A")  
The hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - The relative speed between Allen and Bob is the sum of their speeds.
  - The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is the distance between X and Y divided by the relative speed between them.
  - The distance that Bob covers more than Allen is the product of the time they both traveled after their first meeting and the difference between their speeds.
  - The time it takes for Allen to travel from Y to X and back to Y is twice the time it takes for him to travel from X to Y.
Action: Answer("C")  
Solution:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time be t.
  The relative speed between Allen and Bob is 54 + 78 = 132 kmph.
  Therefore, d = 132t.
  After their first meeting, Allen and Bob continue to travel for the same amount of time until they meet for the second time.
  Let the time it takes for Allen to travel from Y to X and back to Y be 2t.
  Therefore, the time it takes for Bob to travel from X to Y and back to X is also 2t.
  The distance that Bob covers more than Allen is (78 - 54) * 2t = 48t.
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen, so 48t = 48.
  Therefore, t = 1 hour.
  Substituting t = 1 hour into d = 132t, we get d = 132 km.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Speed * Time
  - Time = Distance / Speed
  - When two objects move towards each other, their relative speed is the sum of their individual speeds.
  - When two objects move away from each other, their relative speed is the difference between their individual speeds.
  - Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d km.
  
Solution:
  - Let's assume the time taken by Allen to reach Y is t hours.
  - In that time, Bob covers the distance (d - 48) km towards X.
  - So, the time taken by Bob to reach X is (d - 48) / 78 hours.
  - Now, Allen starts moving towards X from Y. The relative speed of Allen and Bob is (54 + 78) = 132 kmph.
  - So, they will meet after (d - 48) / 132 hours.
  - In that time, Allen covers the distance (54 * t) km towards X.
  - So, the distance covered by Bob in the same time is (d - 48) + (54 * t) km.
  - We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. So, we can write the equation:
        (d - 48) + (54 * t) = (54 * t) + 48
  - Solving the above equation, we get:
        d = 144 km
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - Allen and Bob start from opposite points and move towards each other.
  - Allen covers the same distance as Bob.
  - Allen and Bob meet twice.
  - Allen's speed is 54 kmph and Bob's speed is 78 kmph.
  - Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  
Approach:
  - Let the distance between X and Y be d km.
  - Let the time taken for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time be t hours.
  - Let the time taken for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time be 2t hours.
  - When they meet for the first time, the total distance covered by both of them is d.
  - When they meet for the second time, the total distance covered by both of them is 2d.
  - We can form two equations using the above information and solve for d.
  
Calculations:
  - In the first meeting, Allen covers a distance of 54t km and Bob covers a distance of 78t km.
  - So, 54t + 78t = d
  - 132t = d
  - In the second meeting, Allen covers a distance of 54(2t - t) = 54t km and Bob covers a distance of 78(2t - t) = 78t km.
  - So, 54t + 48 = 78t
  - 24t = 48
  - t = 2
  - Substituting t = 2 in the first equation, we get d = 132t = 264 km.
  
Answer: Answer("A") 
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  - Allen and Bob start from opposite points, move towards each other, and then move away from each other when they meet.
  - Allen's speed is 54 kmph and Bob's speed is 78 kmph.
  - When they meet for the first time, they have covered the same distance.
  - When they meet for the second time, Bob has covered 48 km more than Allen.
  
Approach:
  - Let the distance between X and Y be d km.
  - Let the time taken for Allen to reach Y be t hours.
  - Then, the time taken for Bob to reach X is also t hours.
  - When they meet for the first time, they have covered a total distance of d km.
  - When they meet for the second time, the distance covered by Allen is d km and the distance covered by Bob is 2d - 48 km.
  - Using the formula distance = speed x time, we can write two equations in terms of d and t.
  - Solving these equations will give us the value of d.

Calculation:
  - At 54 kmph, Allen covers d km in d/54 hours.
  - At 78 kmph, Bob covers d km in d/78 hours.
  - When they meet for the first time, the total time taken is d/54 + d/78 hours.
  - When they meet for the second time, Allen covers d km in 2d/54 hours and Bob covers 2d - 48 km in (2d - 48)/78 hours.
  - We can write the following equation based on the distance covered by Allen and Bob:
    2d - 48 = 78 * (2d - 48)/54 - 54 * 2d/54
  - Solving this equation gives d = 126 km.

Answer: Answer("C")

  - The time taken for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time is the same.

- The distance covered by Bob from Y to X and back to X is 2d km.

- The time taken by Bob to cover 2d km at 78 kmph is (2d/78) hours.
- The time taken by Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is (d/66) hours.

- x + 48 = 78 x (2d/78 - d/66) = 4d

Solution:
  - Let's first find the distance covered by Allen in the first leg of his journey.
  - Distance covered by Allen in the first leg = speed x time = 54t.
  - Bob covers the same distance in the same time, so he covers 54t + 48 km in the first leg.
  - Distance between X and Y = d = 54t + 54t + 48 = 108t + 48.
  - Let's find the time it takes for Bob to reach X.
  - Distance covered by Bob in the first leg = speed x time = 78t1.
  - Allen covers the same distance in the same time, so he covers 78t1 - 48 km in the first leg.
  - Let's find the time it takes for Allen to reach X after changing his direction.
  - Distance covered by Allen in the second leg = speed x time = 54t2.
  - Bob covers the same distance in the same time, so he covers 54t2 + 48 km in the second leg.
  - Distance covered by Allen in the second leg = distance covered by Bob in the first leg.
  - Therefore, 54t2 = 78t1 - 48.
  - We can use this equation to substitute t2 in terms of t1.
  - t2 = (78t1 - 48)/54.
  - We know that the total time taken by Allen is t + t2.
  - Therefore, t + t2 = t + (78t1 - 48)/54.
  - Simplifying this equation, we get t2 = (78t1 - 48)/54.
  - Substituting the value of t2 in terms of t1 in the equation for d, we get:
  - d = 108t + 48 = 108t + 78t1 - 48.
  - Simplifying this equation, we get:
  - d = 108t + 78t1 - 48.
  - We know that distance = speed x time.
  - Therefore, d = 54t2 + 48 + 78t1 - 48.
  - Substituting the value of t2 in terms of t1, we get:
  - d = 54(78t1 - 48)/54 + 78t1.
  - Simplifying this equation, we get:
  - d = 78t1 + 78.
  - We know that distance = speed x time.
  - Therefore, d = 78t1 + 54t2.
  - Substituting the value of t2 in terms of t1, we get:
  - d = 78t1 + 54(78t1 - 48)/54.
  - Simplifying this equation, we get:
  - d = 78t1 + 78.
  - We can solve this equation for t1.
  - d - 78 = 78t1.
  - t1 = (d - 78)/78.
  - We can substitute this value of t1 in the equation for d to get the distance between X and Y.
  - d = 78t1 + 78 = 78((d - 78)/78) + 78.
  - Simplifying this equation, we get:
  - d = d - 78 + 78.
  - Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 78 km.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If there is one water lily on the first day, it takes 60 days to fully cover the lake.
  If there are 64 water lilies on the first day, we need to find how many days it will take to fully cover the lake.
  
Solution:
  We can start by finding out how many times the number of water lilies needs to double to reach the fully covered state.
  If there is one water lily on the first day, and the number of lilies doubles every two days, then on the 60th day, the number of lilies would have doubled 30 times (since 60/2 = 30).
  Therefore, the number of lilies on the 60th day would be 2^30.
  If there are 64 water lilies on the first day, we need to find out how many times we need to double 64 to get to 2^30.
  2^6 = 64, so we need to double 6 times to get to 64.
  Therefore, we need to double the number of lilies 30 - 6 = 24 more times to get to 2^30.
  Since the number of lilies doubles every two days, it will take 24 * 2 = 48 days to double the number of lilies 24 more times.
  Therefore, the total number of days it will take to fully cover the lake is 48 + 2 = 50 days.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") 
(Note: The correct answer is not among the choices. The correct answer is 50 days.)
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the number of water lilies after n days is 2^(n/2) times the initial number of water lilies.
  If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies starting from one water lily, then the number of water lilies after 60 days is 2^(60/2) = 2^30.
Action: 
  The number of water lilies after n days starting from 64 water lilies is 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We want to find the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, so we need to solve the equation 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^25.
  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get n/2 = 25.
  Solving for n, we get n = 50.
  Therefore, it takes 50 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies starting from 64 water lilies.

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M travels from City A to City B and takes 4 hours.
  Train N travels from City B to City A and takes 3.5 hours.
  The trains cross each other when their total distance traveled is equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  The distance between City A and City B is the same for both trains.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed
  
Calculation:
  Let's assume the distance between City A and City B is d.
  Let's assume the speed of train M is x.
  Let's assume the speed of train N is y.
  We know that:
  time taken by train M = 4 hours
  time taken by train N = 3.5 hours
  time taken by both trains to cross each other = t
  distance traveled by train M = x * 4
  distance traveled by train N = y * 3.5
  distance traveled by both trains to cross each other = (x + y) * t
  We also know that:
  distance traveled by train M + distance traveled by train N = distance between City A and City B
  x * 4 + y * 3.5 = d
  We can solve for d:
  d = 4x + 3.5y
  We can substitute d in the second equation:
  4x + 3.5y = (x + y) * t
  4x + 3.5y = xt + yt
  4x + 3.5y = (x + y)t
  t = (4x + 3.5y) / (x + y)
  
Action: Answer("C")

  When the two trains cross each other, their total distance traveled is equal to the distance between City A and City B, so we have:
  4sM + 3.5sN = d

  t = 4 - (7 - t) = t - 3
  t = 3
  Now we can use the formula time = distance / speed to find the speed of the two trains:
  sM = d / 4
  sN = d / 3.5
  And we can substitute these values into the equation we derived earlier to solve for "d":
  4(d/4) + 3.5(d/3.5) = d
  d + d = 2d = 14
  d = 7

  t = d / (sM + sN)
  t = 7 / (d/4 + d/3.5)
  t = 7 / (7/4 + 7/3.5)
  t = 56 minutes
  Therefore, the answer is D: 56 min.

Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of all values / number of values.
  Let's call the sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles "S" and the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  We know that (S/10) = 12.2 and ((S+x)/11) = 14.8 (since the average increased by 2.6 tons).
  We can use these two equations to solve for "x".
  Simplifying the second equation, we get S + x = 162.8.
  Substituting the first equation into the second equation, we get 10(12.2) + x = 162.8.
  Solving for "x", we get x = 44.6.

  The amount of clay in the remaining mixture will still be 70% of (10-x) kg.
  The amount of sand in the remaining mixture will be 30% of (10-x) kg + x kg.
  We want the amount of clay and sand to be equal, so we need to solve for x.

  The amount of clay in the remaining mixture = 70% of (10-x) kg
  The amount of sand in the remaining mixture = 30% of (10-x) kg + x kg
  We want the amount of clay and sand to be equal, so:
  70% of (10-x) kg = 30% of (10-x) kg + x kg
  40% of (10-x) kg = x kg
  0.4(10-x) = x
  4 - 0.4x = x
  4 = 1.4x
  x = 40/14 = 20/7

Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre  broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + breadth)
  In this case, perimeter = 340 meters
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot is L and the breadth is B.
  The boundary around the rectangular plot will increase the length and breadth by 2 meters each.
  The cost of gardening 1 square meter is given as 10.
  
Calculation:
  2(L + B) = 340
  L + B = 170
  Length of the increased boundary = L + 2 + L = 2L + 2
  Breadth of the increased boundary = B + 2 + B = 2B + 2
  Area of the increased boundary = (2L + 2) * (2B + 2)
                                 = 4(L + B + 1)
                                 = 4(170 + 1)
                                 = 684
  Cost of gardening 1 square meter = 10
  Cost of gardening the increased boundary = 684 * 10 = 6840
  
  Total cost of gardening = Cost of gardening the increased boundary
                           = 6840

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is given by the formula: 2(L+W) = 340
  Therefore, L+W = 170
  The cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is the same as finding the area of the rectangular plot with dimensions (L+2) and (W+2) and then multiplying it by 10.
  The area of the rectangular plot is given by the formula: L*W
  The area of the rectangular plot with dimensions (L+2) and (W+2) is given by the formula: (L+2)(W+2)
  Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is: 10[(L+2)(W+2) - L*W]

Action: Answer("C")  
To find the cost of gardening 1-meter-wide boundary around the rectangular plot, we need to calculate the area of the boundary and then multiply it by 10.
  Perimeter = 2(L+B) = 340
  L+B = 170
  Area of the rectangular plot = L x B
  Area of the rectangular plot with the boundary = (L+2) x (B+2)
  Area of the boundary = (L+2) x 1 + (B+2) x 1 = L + B + 4
  Area of the boundary for all four sides = 2(L+B+4)
  Area of the boundary for 1-meter-wide boundary = 2(L+B+4) x 1
  Total area to be gardened = 2(L+B+4) x 1
  Total cost = 10 x Total area to be gardened
  Substituting L+B=170, we get
  Total cost = 10 x 2(170+4)
  Total cost = 10 x 348
  Total cost = 3480
  Cost of gardening 1-meter-wide boundary around the rectangular plot = Total cost - Cost of gardening the rectangular plot
  Cost of gardening 1-meter-wide boundary around the rectangular plot = 3480 - (L x B x 10)
  Since we don't know the values of L and B, we cannot determine the exact cost of gardening 1-meter-wide boundary around the rectangular plot. However, we can say that the answer is not "None of these". Therefore, the most likely answer is C: 3440.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) x 100
  Cost Price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  Selling price is the price at which the merchant sold the oranges.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450, so the cost price per kg is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold the oranges at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg, so the selling price per kg is Rs. 7.50.
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. (7.50 - 5) = Rs. 2.50 per kg.
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) x 100 = (2.50/5) x 100 = 50%.

Action: Answer("A")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joes fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's start by defining some variables:
- Let's call Joe's age "J"
- Let's call Joe's sister's age "S"
- Let's call Joe's father's age "F"

From the first sentence, we know that:
J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that:
J + F = 2(S)

From the third sentence, we know that:
F = 2(S - J)

We can use the second equation to solve for S:
S = (J + F) / 2

We can substitute this expression for S into the third equation:
F = 2((J + F) / 2 - J)
F = J

Now we have two equations with two variables:
J + S + F = 100
F = J

We can substitute F = J into the first equation:
J + S + F = 100
J + S + J = 100
2J + S = 100

We can substitute S = (J + F) / 2 into this equation:
2J + S = 100
2J + (J + F) / 2 = 100
4J + J + F = 200
5J + F = 200

We can substitute F = J into this equation:
5J + F = 200
5J + J = 200
6J = 200
J = 33.33 (repeating)

Now we can find F:
F = J
F = 33.33 (repeating)

Action: Answer("None of the above") 
(Note: None of the answer choices match the calculated value of Joe's father's age, which is approximately 33.33)
Response 1:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father (i.e. F), his sister (i.e. S) will be twice as old as she is now (i.e. 2S). We can set up an equation:

J + F = 2S

We can simplify this equation by substituting the first equation into it:

J + F = 2S
J + F = 2(100 - J - F)
J + F = 200 - 2J - 2F
3J + 3F = 200

Now we have two equations with two variables:

J + S + F = 100
3J + 3F = 200

We can solve for J and F using any method of our choice. Let's use substitution:

J + S + F = 100
J + F = 2S

Solving the second equation for S, we get:

S = (J + F)/2

Substituting this into the first equation, we get:

J + (J + F)/2 + F = 100
2J + J + F + 2F = 200
3J + 3F = 200

Dividing both sides by 3, we get:

J + F = 200/3

Substituting this into the equation J + F = 2S, we get:

200/3 = 4S/2
S = 100/6

Substituting J and S into the equation J + S + F = 100, we get:

100/6 + 100/3 + F = 100
F = 200/3 - 100/6
F = 50

Therefore, Joe's father is 50 years old.

9J = 100

F = 3J
F = 33 1/3

Response 4:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

or

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father:

F = 2(S - F)

or

3F = 2S

We now have three equations with three variables. We can solve for one variable in terms of the other two and substitute into the other equations to get a system of two equations with two variables. 

From equation 3, we have:

S = (3/2)F

Substituting this into equation 2, we get:

J = 2(3/2)F - F = 2F

Substituting these into equation 1, we get:

2F + (3/2)F + F = 100

Response 5:
Let's start by defining some variables:
- Let's call Joe's age "J"
- Let's call Joe's sister's age "S"
- Let's call Joe's father's age "F"

From the first sentence, we know that:
J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that:
J + F = 2(S)

From the third sentence, we know that:
F = 2(S - J)

We can use the second equation to solve for S in terms of J and F:
S = (J + F)/2

We can substitute this expression for S into the third equation:
F = 2((J + F)/2 - J)
F = 2(F/2 - J)
F = F - 2J
2J = 0
J = 0

This doesn't make sense, since Joe's age cannot be zero. Therefore, there must be an error in the problem statement.
Response 6:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100 

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

We can simplify this to:

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age when Joe's sister was as old as his father "x". At that time, Joe's father was F - x years old, and his sister was S - x years old. So we have:

F - x = 2(S - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

2x = F - S

Now we have three equations with three variables. We can solve for one variable in terms of the other two, and then substitute into the other equations to get a system of two equations with two variables. 

Let's solve for S in terms of J and F from the equation J = 2S - F:

S = (J + F)/2

Now we can substitute this into the first equation:

J + (J + F)/2 + F = 100

Simplifying this equation, we get:

3J/2 + 3F/2 = 100

Dividing both sides by 3, we get:

J/2 + F/2 = 50/3

Now we can substitute S = (J + F)/2 and S = (F - J/2) into the equation 2x = F - S:

2x = F - (J + F)/2

2x = F/2 - J/2

4x = F - J

Substituting 4x = F - J into the equation J/2 + F/2 = 50/3, we get:

(4x + J)/2 + (4x - J)/2 = 50/3

Simplifying this equation, we get:

4x = 25

So x = 25/4. 

Now we can substitute x = 25/4 into the equation 2x = F - S:

Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

We can simplify this to:

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age when Joe's sister was as old as his father "x". At that time, Joe's father was F - x years old, and his sister was S - x years old. So we have:

F - x = 2(S - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

2x = F - S

Now we have three equations with three variables. We can solve for one variable in terms of the other two, and then substitute that expression into the other equations to get a system of two equations with two variables. 

Let's solve for S in terms of J and F from the equation J = 2S - F:

S = (J + F)/2

Now we can substitute this expression for S into the other two equations:

J + (J + F)/2 + F = 100

J + F = 2(J + F)/2

Simplifying the second equation, we get:

J + F = J + F

This equation is true, so we don't get any new information from it. Let's simplify the first equation:

J + J/2 + F + F/2 = 100

3J/2 + 3F/2 = 100

J + F = 100/3 * 2

J + F = 200/3

Now we have two equations with two variables:

J + F = 200/3

2x = F - S

We can solve for F in terms of x from the second equation:

F = 2x + S

Substituting the expression for S from earlier:

F = 2x + (J + F)/2

Multiplying both sides by 2:

2F = 4x + J + F

Simplifying:

F = 4x + J

Now we can substitute this expression for F into the first equation:

J + (4x + J) = 200/3

Simplifying:

5J + 12x = 200/3

We need to find the value of F, which is 4x + J. We can solve for J in terms of x from the equation above:

5J = 200/3 - 12x

J = (200/3 - 12x)/5

Now we can substitute this expression for J into the equation for F:

F = 4x + (200/3 - 12x)/5

Simplifying:

F = (20x + 200/3 - 36x)/5

F = (200/3 - 16x)/5

We want to find the value of x that makes F an integer. Let's try some values of x:

If x = 1, then F = (200/3 - 16)/5 = 56/5, which is not an integer.
If x = 2, then F = (200/3 - 32)/5 = 44/5, which is not an integer.
If x = 3, then F = (200/3 - 48)/5 = 32/5, which is an integer.

So the answer is F = 32/5 * 5 = 32.

Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let's use J for Joe's age, S for his sister's age, and F for his father's age.

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J = 66 - F

And we can use the equation F = 2S - x to find Joe's father's age:

F = 2(33) - x

We need to find x, the age when Joe's sister was as old as his father. We know that the age difference between Joe and his sister is the same as the age difference between Joe and his father, so:

F - S = J - S

So Joe's father is 32 years old.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Tails (20 - x) times.
  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher (20 - x) times.
  The total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan is 2x.
  The total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher is 3(20 - x) = 60 - 3x.
  Since neither of them won or lost any amount, we can set the two amounts equal to each other and solve for x.
  2x = 60 - 3x
  5x = 60
  x = 12
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  For each head, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  For each tail, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, neither of them won or lost any amount.

  Therefore, 2x = 60-3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.

Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - Distance = Speed x Time
  - Let d be the distance between A and B.
  - Let t1 be the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B.
  - Let t2 be the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A.
  - We know that t2 = t1 - 3 (since he has 3 hours left in his trip when he is 70 miles away from B).
  - We also know that d = 70t1 (since he drove at 70 mph from A to B) and d = 90t2 (since he drove at 90 mph from B to A).
Action: 
  - We can use the two equations above to solve for t1 and t2 in terms of d:
    - t1 = d/70
    - t2 = d/90 + 3
  - We can substitute these expressions for t1 and t2 into the equation d/70 - 3 = d/90:
    - d/70 - 3 = d/90
    - Multiplying both sides by 630 (the least common multiple of 70 and 90) gives:
    - 9d - 1890 = 7d
    - Solving for d gives:
    - d = 630 miles
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 630 miles.
Answer: Answer("E") None of the above. The correct answer is 630 miles.

  - This means that t1 = t2 + 3 = 1.
  - Finally, we can use d = 70t1 to solve for d.
    - d = 70(1) = 70.
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 70 miles.

  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to travel from B to A "u"

  - We also know that Kevin was 70 miles away from B, 3 hours before the end of his trip.
  
Calculations:
  - We can set up two equations based on the information we have:
    - d = 70t  (distance from A to B)
    - d = 90u  (distance from B to A)
  - We also know that Kevin was 70 miles away from B, 3 hours before the end of his trip. This means that:
    - t + u - 3 = d/70
    - We can substitute the first two equations into this equation to get:
      - t + u - 3 = d/70
      - t + u - 3 = t/70 * 70 + u/90 * 70
      - t + u - 3 = t + 7u/9
      - 2t = 2u/9 + 3
      - We can simplify this to:
        - 18t = 2u + 27
        - 9t = u + 13.5
  - Now we can substitute this into one of the first two equations to get:
    - d = 70t
    - d = 90(u+13.5)
    - 70t = 90(u+13.5)
    - 7t = 9(u+13.5)
    - 7t = 9u + 121.5
    - We can substitute 9t = u + 13.5 into this equation to get:
      - 7t = 9(9t - 13.5) + 121.5
      - 7t = 81t - 121.5 + 121.5
      - 74t = 121.5
      - t = 1.64
  - Now we can substitute t into one of the first two equations to get:
    - d = 70t
    - d = 70(1.64)
    - d = 114.8

Action: Answer("E")  None of the above. The correct answer is 114.8.

Topic: Math
Question: I know a 5 digit number having a property that with a 1 after it, it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it.
What is that number?
Choices:
  A: 42857
  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567
  E: 43566
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To solve the problem, we need to use algebra. Let's assume that the 5-digit number is represented by "abcde". 
  According to the problem, if we add a 1 after the number, we get "abcde1", which is three times as large as the number with a 1 before it, represented by "1abcde". 
  Therefore, we can write the following equation: 
  10 * abcde + 1 = 3 * (100000 + abcde)
  Solving for abcde, we get:
  abcde = 42857
  A: 42857 is the correct answer.
  B: 32456 is not the correct answer.
  C: 76523 is not the correct answer.
  D: 24567 is not the correct answer.
  E: 43566 is not the correct answer.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Let the 5 digit number be abcde.
  With a 1 after it, the number becomes abcde1 and is three times as large as the original number abcde.
  With a 1 before it, the number becomes 1abcde and is 1/3 as large as the original number abcde.
  We can set up the following equations:
    abcde1 = 3 * abcde
    1abcde = 1/3 * abcde
  We know that a 5 digit number cannot start with 0.
  Therefore, a can only be 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, or 9.
  We can try each of these values for a and see which one satisfies the equations.
  Trying a = 1, we get abcde1 = 3 * abcde => 1bcde1 = 3 * bcde => 10001b + 1000c + 100d + 10e + 1 = 3000b + 300c + 30d + 3e => 999b + 200c + 70d + 2e = 1.
  Since b, c, d, and e are digits, we know that 999b + 200c + 70d + 2e <= 999 * 9 + 200 * 9 + 70 * 9 + 2 * 9 = 9999.
  Therefore, there are only a few possible values for b, c, d, and e that satisfy the equation.
  Trying each of these values, we find that the only solution is abcde = 42857.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let the number of employees in the organization be x.
Then, the amount contributed by each employee is (600000/x) rupees.
If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution per employee would be (600000+24000)/x = 624000/x.
Equating the two expressions, we get:
600000/x + 60 = 624000/x
Solving for x, we get:
x = 400
Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's assume that there are "n" employees in the organization and each employee contributes "x" amount of money. 

From the problem, we know that:
nx = 600000   ----(1) (since the total contribution is Rs. 6 lakh)
and
n(x+60) = 624000 ----(2) (since the total contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh if each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra)

Expanding equation (2), we get:
nx + 60n = 624000

Substituting the value of nx from equation (1), we get:
600000 + 60n = 624000

Solving for "n", we get:
n = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization and each employee contributes 'x' amount of money. 

So, the total amount collected by 'n' employees is n*x. 

According to the problem, 

n*x = 6,00,000  ----(1)

If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the total contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. 

So, the new contribution by 'n' employees is n*(x+60).

According to the problem, 

n*(x+60) = 6,24,000  ----(2)

We need to find the value of 'n'.

Let's solve the above two equations to find the value of 'n'.

n*x = 6,00,000  ----(1)

n*(x+60) = 6,24,000  ----(2)

Subtracting equation (1) from equation (2), we get:

n*(x+60) - n*x = 24,000

n*60 = 24,000

n = 24,000/60

n = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.

Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
Then, each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.
The total number of recipients is 5+4+2 = 11.
So, we have the equation: 
5x + 4(4x) + 2x = 8600
Simplifying the equation, we get:
23x = 8600
x = 374
So, each daughter receives 4x = 4*374 = 1496.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.

  A: 1584
  B: 2520

Response 0:

  A: 1584 = 7/8 * x is not the correct answer because it is the value of 7/8 of the number, not 7/18.
  B: 2520 = 7/8 * x is not the correct answer because it is the value of 7/8 of the number, not 7/18.
  C: 1728 = 7/8 * x is not the correct answer because it is the value of 7/8 of the number, not 7/18.
  D: 1656 = 7/8 * x - 770 is the correct answer because it is the value of 7/18 of the number minus 770, which is the difference between the two values.
